## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P. This is a fundamental problem in population ecology where various growth models describe how populations change based on density-dependent and density-independent factors.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing with time)
- Logistic with time-dependent rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * exp(c2 * t) (time-modulated logistic)
- Richards growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth curve)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- dP/dt proportional to P indicates exponential/Malthusian growth; the coefficient sign determines growth vs decline
- A term of form P*(1 - c*P) signals logistic-type density dependence with a carrying capacity K = 1/c
- Logarithmic coupling log(c/P) with P suggests Gompertz-type asymmetric growth where decline in rate is proportional to log of remaining capacity
- Multiple roots in dP_dt as a function of P (e.g., cubic polynomial in P) indicate bistability or Allee effects with multiple equilibria
- Time appearing only inside periodic functions (sin, cos) suggests seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing rather than secular trends
- Rational forms like P/(1+c*P) indicate contest competition where per-capita resources saturate at high density
- Fractional powers of P (e.g., P**0.75) often arise from metabolic scaling laws relating body size/population to energy use
- Negative constant terms independent of P represent density-independent mortality or harvesting pressure
- Products of (P - threshold) terms create critical population sizes below which growth becomes negative (strong Allee effect)
- Time appearing in exponential factors exp(c*t) multiplying growth terms suggests deteriorating or improving environmental conditions over time

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$0.8678(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185)P + 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P$$

Let me expand the cubic term:
$$(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P^2/(6.058 \times 14.185)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P^2/85.90$$

Multiplying by P:
$$= -P + P^2(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P^3/85.90$$

Then multiplying by 0.8678:
$$= -0.8678P + 0.8678P^2(0.0705 + 0.1651) - 0.8678P^3/85.90$$
$$= -0.8678P + 0.8678 \times 0.2356 \times P^2 - 0.01010 P^3$$

Adding the other terms (+0.8678P^{1/3} + 0.8678P):
$$= 0.8678 P^{1/3} + (-0.8678 + 0.8678)P + 0.2044 P^2 - 0.01010 P^3$$

So the linear terms cancel! The GT simplifies to:
$$\text{GT} = 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.2044 P^2 - 0.01010 P^3$$

This is: **P^{1/3} (with coefficient) + P^2 (with coefficient) + P^3 (with coefficient)**

Wait, let me double-check: c6 = 1/3, so P^{c6} = P^{1/3}, not P^{1/4}.

The GT has basis functions: **P^{1/3}, P^2, P^3**

Now let me check candidates. Many candidates use P^{1/4} or P^{0.25}. The GT uses P^{1/3}. These are different basis functions and cannot be made equal by adjusting constants.

Let me verify: P^{1/4} тЙа P^{1/3} for all P. These are linearly independent. So any candidate with P^{1/4} instead of P^{1/3} is a NO MATCH (unless there's another term that could compensate, but by linear independence of power functions, this is impossible).

Let me now systematically check each candidate:

**Candidates with P^{1/4} or P^{0.25}:** 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 9, 11, 12, 17, 24, 25, 29, 30, 32, 33, 34, 35
All these are **NO MATCH** because P^{1/4} тЙа P^{1/3}.

**Candidates with P^{c_k} where c_k is free:**
These could set c_k = 1/3.

Let me check the remaining candidates that have a free power P^{c_k}:

**Candidate 8:** P┬│c0 + P┬▓c1 + Pc2/(P+1) + Pc3/(P+1) + P^{c4}┬╖c5┬╖log(Pc6+1) + c7/(P+1)

**Candidate 13:** Combines to P^4┬╖c0/(Pc1+1) + ... This is a rational function. Let me simplify with common denominator (Pc1+1):

[PA+B]/(P+1) = A - (A-B)/(P+1). For this to equal 0 (since GT has no such terms), set A=0 and B=0. Then we get P┬│c0 + P┬▓c1 + c5┬╖P^{1/3}. This matches GT! тЬУ
